# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Producer to Broker Network Write Chain

## Your Task

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

Perfect! I've successfully traced the Kafka ProduceRequest chain from KafkaProducer.send() to the broker's log append and created the answer.json file.

## Summary

I've identified and documented the complete chain of how a Kafka ProduceRequest travels through the system:

**Producer Side (Client):**
1. **KafkaProducer.send()** - Entry point that delegates to doSend() which calls RecordAccumulator.append()
2. **RecordAccumulator.append()** - Buffers records into batches in memory
3. **Sender.sendProducerData()** - Background thread that drains batches and initiates sending
4. **NetworkClient.send()** - Transmits the ProduceRequest over the network

**Broker Side (Server):**
5. **KafkaApis.handleProduceRequest()** - Receives and validates the incoming ProduceRequest
6. **ReplicaManager.handleProduceAppend()** - Performs transaction verification and setup
7. **ReplicaManager.appendRecords()** - Appends records to the broker's replicated log

All files are from the **github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489** repository (apache/kafka). The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbol names, and a detailed narrative explanation of the data flow.

When called with a ProducerRecord, it delegates to the internal doSend() method which calls RecordAccumulator.append().\\n\\n2. **RecordAccumulator.append()** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java:275) - Accumulates producer records into batches. It buffers records in memory and groups them by partition, creating batch objects when needed. The records are held in MemoryRecords format.\\n\\n3. **Sender.sendProducerData()** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java:357) - The background sender thread method that prepares data for sending. It checks which partitions are ready to send, drains batches from the RecordAccumulator using the accumulator.drain() method, and calls sendProduceRequests() to send the batches.\\n\\n4. **NetworkClient.send()** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/NetworkClient.java:541) - Sends the ClientRequest (containing the ProduceRequest) over the network to the broker. It constructs a NetworkSend object and adds it to the selector for transmission.\\n\\n**Broker Side (Server):**\\n\\n5. **KafkaApis.handleProduceRequest()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaApis.scala:388) - Receives the incoming ProduceRequest from the network. It validates authorization, handles transaction state, and then delegates to ReplicaManager.handleProduceAppend() for the actual record appending.\\n\\n6. **ReplicaManager.handleProduceAppend()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaManager.scala:731) - An intermediate handler that performs transaction verification and validation before calling appendRecords(). It processes transactional information, validates records, and sets up callbacks for response handling.\\n\\n7. **ReplicaManager.appendRecords()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaManager.scala:674) - The final destination method that appends the records to the broker's replicated log. This method handles the actual log append operation, manages replication, and executes delayed operations.\\n\\nThe complete flow traces how a producer batch accumulated from user send() calls is serialized as a ProduceRequest, transmitted over the network, received by the broker's request handler, and ultimately appended to the broker's log through the ReplicaManager.\"\n}\n",
